    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="338e8685a1ee468b87b22730a2cab4d5">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'beeb6ccb-753f-401b-be30-4df5041beefb'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d164363862" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>The binder's choice holds immense significance in the quest for robust electrochemical performances of lithium/sodium-ion battery's (LIB/SIB) electrodes. Conventional PVDF binder is a passive polymer lacking the ability to transport Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> and facilitate ion kinetics. This limitation poses constraints in achieving high specific capacity, fast charging, and long cycle life. Herein, a novel water-soluble concentrated imidazolium functionalized poly(ionic liquid), poly(oxycarbonylmethylene 1-allyl-3-methyimidazolium) (PMAI) is synthesized, and evaluated it as binder in LIB/SIB. PMAI-based anodic-half cell exhibits excellent electrochemical performance, achieving higher capacities (297 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> at 1C for LIBs and 250 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> at 60 mAg<sup>−1</sup> for SIBs) and good cycle stability (80 % capacity retention after 750 cycles for LIBs; 96% capacity retention after 200 cycles for SIBs), compared to PVDF binder. In addition, PMAI/Gr delivers a higher discharge capacity of 85 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> than PVDF/Gr with 47 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> at 5C. PMAI-containing electrodes show better rate capability at different current densities than PVDF binder in LIB/SIB. The enhanced ion diffusion coefficient, lower resistance and decreased activation energy of desolvation, are ascribed to densely polar ionic liquid groups along the polymer and formation of a functionalized SEI via binder reduction. The novel PMAI binder's design and full-cell examination confirm its potential in secondary-ion battery applications.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403071-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>In addressing modern societal demands for electronic devices characterized by enhanced efficiency and performance, a need for high-performance, affordable and safe energy storage technologies has become increasingly crucial.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0001_R_d164363756e306" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">1</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0004_R_d164363756e306" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Over the past thirty years, secondary-ion batteries have served as attractive power sources, offering applications ranging from small portable devices to transportation systems. As global demand for lithium/sodium is set to rise, the importance of LIBs/SIBs, which are currently the most competitive battery technology, becomes increasingly evident. However, concerns have emerged regarding the sustainability of lithium as a resource, driven by problems related to its scarcity, cost, concentrated geographical distribution and battery performance of existing LIB technology. These drawbacks led to research hovering around SIBs, which has gathered attention, mainly due to the abundant and readily available sodium in nature, low cost, and high electrochemical potential.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0005_R_d164363756e311" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5">5</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0012_R_d164363756e311" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Chem. Lett.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the larger sodium ionic radius has created challenges related to phase stability, ion kinetics and interphase formation. Consequently, the quest for cost-effective, high-performance electrode materials for LIBs/SIBs still requires attention inspite of being extensively researched. Recent interests in LIBs and SIBs are in exploring various cathodes, such as layered transition metal oxides<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0013_R_d164363756e316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Royal Soc. Chem.">13</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0016_R_d164363756e316" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Royal Soc. Chem.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and polyanion-type compounds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0017_R_d164363756e322" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">17</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0021_R_d164363756e322" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Simultaneously, potential anode materials have been reported encompassing graphite,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0022_R_d164363756e327" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Royal Soc. Chem">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> silicon,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0023_R_d164363756e333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Chem. Eng. J. Adv.">23</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0024_R_d164363756e333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> hard carbon (HC),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0025_R_d164363756e338" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J Mater Chem A Mater.">25</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0026_R_d164363756e338" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Power Sources">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> soft carbon,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0027_R_d164363756e343" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Electrochem. Commun.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> metal oxide,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0028_R_d164363756e349" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Chem. Commun.">28</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0029_R_d164363756e349" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angewandte Chemie International Edition">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> transition metal sulfide,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0030_R_d164363756e354" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nanomicro. Lett.">30</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0031_R_d164363756e354" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Mater. Chem.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> transition metal dichalcogenides<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0032_R_d164363756e359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano Energy">32</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0033_R_d164363756e359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Ionics">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and nanocomposite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0034_R_d164363756e365" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Chem. Commun.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Lithium/sodium alloy anode materials offer significantly higher capacities among the anode materials. However, they exhibit substantial volume expansion during intercalation, leading to structural damage and poor cycle durability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0035_R_d164363756e370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, graphite and hard carbon remain promising, considering the cost implications for potential scaling up, and stand out as the most promising anode material.</p>
         
         <p>Despite carbon materials being promising anode for LIBs/SIBs, these electrodes face challenges, including poor specific capacity and capacity retention. These issues are caused by the uneven, thick, and poor mechanical strength of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) at the electrode surface and in ionic conduction along the electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0036_R_d164363756e378" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Energy Environ. Sci.">36</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0037_R_d164363756e378" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Carbon">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Significant approaches have been directed towards crafting better SEI in SIBs by optimizing defects,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0038_R_d164363756e383" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Battery Energy">38</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0039_R_d164363756e383" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Energy Adv.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> artificial SEI,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0040_R_d164363756e388" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Nano Energy">40</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0041_R_d164363756e388" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> dopant/structural modification,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0042_R_d164363756e394" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - J. Electroanal. Chem.">42</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0043_R_d164363756e394" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Solid State Sci.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> presodiation<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0044_R_d164363756e399" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and additives.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0045_R_d164363756e405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - ChemElectroChem">45</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0046_R_d164363756e405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Power Sources">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, these methods involve intricate synthetic routes, are sensitive to experimental conditions, have high costs and lack desirable scalability. Hence, functional binders can play a crucial role in influencing the composition of the SEI,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0047_R_d164363756e410" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Electrochim. Acta">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> stability and irreversible capacity loss of LIBs/SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0048_R_d164363756e415" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Chem. Mater.">48</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0049_R_d164363756e415" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - J. Power Sources">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Conventional polymer binders such as poly(vinylidene fluoride) (PVDF) and styrene-butadiene rubber (SBR) are non-ionic conducting polymer binders. These binders encounter more significant challenges when employed in high-capacity electrodes that undergo substantial volume changes during cycling, resulting in electrode fractures and delamination.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0050_R_d164363756e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Acc. Chem. Res.">50</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0051_R_d164363756e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Electrochem. Commun.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> PVDF also needs environmentally hazardous organic solvent N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) for making electrode slurry.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0052_R_d164363756e427" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">52</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0054_R_d164363756e427" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Brandell et&nbsp;al. reported that PVDF infiltrates pores of various dimensions, significantly diminishing the surface area and pore volume accessible to electrolytes after cell fabrication.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0055_R_d164363756e432" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - J. Phys. Chem. C">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Lithiation/delithiation or sodiation/desodiation occurs by the transport of ions from the electrolyte into the electrode indicating the importance of electrolyte penetration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0056_R_d164363756e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Mater. Today Chem.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Thus, developing novel binders with better mechanical adhesion, Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> transport/conducting abilities, enhanced surface compatibilities, and self-healing properties will enhance rate capability and long cycling stability in LIBs/SIBs. Hence, a novel binder that aligns with the pragmatic requirements of industrial manufacturing is highly desired.</p>
         
         <p>Ionic liquids (IL) are molten salts comprising organic cations and organic/inorganic anions with melting points lower than 100&nbsp;°C. Some promising properties of IL are high ionic conductivity, better electrochemical stability and low volatility, leading to their use in many dye-sensitized solar cells,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0057_R_d164363756e450" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Nat. Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> capacitors,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0058_R_d164363756e455" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Electrochim. Acta">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> light emitting devices<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0059_R_d164363756e460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and electrolytes in lithium-ion batteries.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0060_R_d164363756e466" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Polymers containing IL moieties have been used as polymer electrolytes for various applications.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0061_R_d164363756e471" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Electrochim. Acta">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Poly(ionic liquid)s (PIL) are ionic polymers consisting of a polymer backbone with cationic or anionic side chains bonded to an opposite ionic species of ionic liquids. PILs are an emerging class of functional group polymers. These polymers are gaining increasing interest due to their distinct chemical and physical characteristics, derived from their ability to retain IL's properties while incorporating polymer's inherent attributes. The advantages of such polymer are better ionic conductivity, flexibility and wide electrochemical stability window.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0062_R_d164363756e477" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - J. Power Sources">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Few works based on the PILs have been reported in the field of binders for LIBs such as thiazolium-type PILs,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0063_R_d164363756e482" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Macro Lett.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> poly(vinylimidazolium) nanoparticle PILs<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0064_R_d164363756e487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and imidazolium-based PILs,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0065_R_d164363756e493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - RSC Adv.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> poly(diallyldimethylammonium) based binders with fluorinated<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0066_R_d164363756e498" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - Mater. Today Chem.">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and non-fluorinated<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0067_R_d164363756e503" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Adv. Energy Sustain. Res.">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> counter anions for cathode and PIL nanoparticles based on 1-vinyl-3-alkyl imidazolium<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e509" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and poly[vinylbenzylallylimidazolium bis(trifluoromethane)sulfonylimide]<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0053_R_d164363756e514" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> for anode. While there are no reports on PIL as binders for HC in SIBs, only a few binders for HC have been reported to date, such as poly(vinylidene fluoride),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0051_R_d164363756e519" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Electrochem. Commun.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0051_R_d164363756e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Electrochem. Commun.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> chondroitin sulfate A,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0069_R_d164363756e530" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Adv. Energy Mater.">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> sodium lignosulfonate<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0070_R_d164363756e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">70</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and trifunctional sodium alginate/polyethylene oxide.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0071_R_d164363756e541" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In brief, not much work was carried out on PIL for graphite and HC to enhance the specific capacity, rate capability and long-cycle stability by improving ion channels into the electrode, enhancing the wettability of the electrolyte on the electrode for faster ion diffusion kinetics, or lower the activation energy of desolvation. Therefore, a suitable dense functional group binder is desired to improve the ion kinetics and SEI, impacting the electrochemical performance of batteries.</p>
         
         <p>This study reports a novel densely functionalized poly(ionic liquid) (DFPIL) binder incorporating high-density oxycarbonyl 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium functional groups. The DFPIL, designated poly(oxycarbonylmethylene 1-allyl-3-methyimidazolium) (PMAI), is a polymethylene based polymer, featuring a rigid polymer backbone that distinguishes it from polyethylene-based binders, suggesting unique properties.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0072_R_d164363756e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - J. Macromol. Sci.: Part A – Chem.">72</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0073_R_d164363756e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Polymer Bulletin">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The dense arrangement of consecutive functional groups within the PIL is anticipated to enhance ionic conductivity by forming ion channels and transporting ions across the edges of the graphite layers, thereby increasing the specific capacity of the LIBs/SIBs. The superior wettability of PIL with the electrolyte, coupled with polar functional groups, is expected to boost ion mobility by forming a PIL/electrolyte heterojunction at the interface.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0063_R_d164363756e555" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Macro Lett.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This phenomenon will likely reduce the activation energy associated with ion desolvation and influence electrolyte decomposition.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0064_R_d164363756e560" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the imidazolium group exhibits reduction at a lower potential, facilitating the formation of a more effective SEI and promoting adhesion to graphite upon reduction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e566" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, considering the positive impact the dense functional group will pose for enhancing the LIB's/SIB's electrochemical performances, PMAI was used as a binder for anode. In the direction of commercialization of better LIB/SIB technology, rheology and various electrochemical studies were carried out to study the PMAI's effect on SEI, electrode morphology after cycling and galvanostatic charge-discharge and compared with commercial counterpart PVDF binder.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403071-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403071-sec-0030-title">2.1 Synthesis and Physical Characterization of PMAI</h3>
            
            <p>We synthesized novel high-density oxycarbonyl 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium functional groups containing PIL, as represented in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0001">1</a>. The three-step process includes bulk radical polymerization followed by base-catalyzed ester hydrolysis and, lastly, neutralization reaction. The use of 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium is assigned to its superior thermal stability, diminished viscosities, improved ionic conductivity, and wide potential window.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0074_R_d164363756e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Macromolecules">74</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0075_R_d164363756e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - J. Mol. Liq.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The pH was found to be about 7.0, indicating the initial confirmation of polymer formation. (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Further, the chemical structure was tested using <sup>1</sup>H NMR spectra, as shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0002">2a</a>. The methine proton of the polymer main chain appeared at 2.98&nbsp;ppm, and the signals of the imidazolium cation unit are assigned in the spectra. For comparison of <sup>1</sup>H NMR and <sup>13</sup>C NMR of PMAI, poly(ethoxycarbonylmethylene) and poly(hydroxycarbonylmethylene) <sup>1</sup>H NMR and <sup>13</sup>C NMR were obtained as shown in Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information) respectively. Peak integration of methine and methylene (proton of imidazolium unit) peaks was performed to evaluate each carboxylate unit interacting with an imidazolium unit. The integration ratio of the proton was determined to be 1:2 of methine to methylene proton peak, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information), proving that the reaction is complete. The <sup>13</sup>C NMR spectrum of PMAI featured all carbon atoms of the polymer, wherein the characteristic methine and methylene carbon peaks appeared at 62.4&nbsp;ppm and 30&nbsp;ppm, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0002">2b</a>). FT-IR spectroscopy revealed a board band centered at 3500 cm<sup>−1</sup> for COO<sup>−</sup>AmIm<sup>+</sup> stretching and a carbonyl peak of carboxylate at 1725 cm<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0002">2c</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0063_R_d164363756e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Macro Lett.">63</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0076_R_d164363756e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Imidazolium unit is characterized by the presence of C<span class="icomoon"></span>N stretching vibration at 1582 cm<sup>−1</sup>, C-H unsymmetrical bending vibration<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0077_R_d164363756e650" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Mater. Chem. Phys.">77</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0078_R_d164363756e650" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - ACS Omega">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> at 1157 cm<sup>−1</sup> and C═C<span class="icomoon"></span>H at 3151 cm<sup>−1</sup>. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information) presents PFA's MALDI-TOF mass data, revealing that the polymer has continuous carboxylic molecules. For example, the ≈44&nbsp;g mol<sup>−1</sup> difference in the 1007.61 and 1051.93 m/z values in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information) for PFA is equal to the molecular weight of -COOH functional groups of the polymer. TGA of the resulting PMAI polymer was carried out to determine the thermal stability (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). The initial 10&nbsp;wt% decomposition temperature is ≈150&nbsp;°C. This indicates the binder stability at higher operating temperatures of LIB/SIB. Characterization of PMAI revealed the formation of the polymer through this novel synthetic route, paving the way for subsequent potential applications.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/098fcd70-8bf9-40ba-b57a-ebf4b5e7c751/aenm202403071-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/098fcd70-8bf9-40ba-b57a-ebf4b5e7c751/aenm202403071-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f51f2b71-bdf6-4db9-928b-3cbe29312587/aenm202403071-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/098fcd70-8bf9-40ba-b57a-ebf4b5e7c751/aenm202403071-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic illustration of PMAI synthesis.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2d53a4ae-618a-4d17-a9fe-5ae26715bc75/aenm202403071-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/2d53a4ae-618a-4d17-a9fe-5ae26715bc75/aenm202403071-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6c922f5c-3268-43aa-8ea2-a7f8231aaa11/aenm202403071-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2d53a4ae-618a-4d17-a9fe-5ae26715bc75/aenm202403071-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) <sup>1</sup>H NMR (400&nbsp;MHz, D<sub>2</sub>O), b) <sup>13</sup>C NMR (100&nbsp;MHz, D<sub>2</sub>O), c) FT-IR spectra of PMAI. d) Load versus Displacement of electrode peel test containing different binders.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The ability to maintain a stable structure even after extended cycling is attributed to strong adhesion between the current collector and active material using a functional binder, ensuring structural stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0079" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0079_R_d164363756e721" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 79 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">79</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Consequently, the 180° peel test investigated the strong PMAI adhesion to active material and copper foil, correlating to stable electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0080" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0080_R_d164363756e726" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 80 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">80</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0002">2d</a> illustrates the force versus displacement profile, revealing that the average force exerted by a PMAI-based electrode was determined to be 10.9 N for PMAI/Gr and 11.0 N for PMAI/HC, whereas that of PVDF-based electrode was 9.8 N for PVDF/Gr and 9.9 N for PVDF/HC. The strong adhesion of the high-density functional group polymer binder PMAI is due to the strong interaction of the functional polar group of the binder with the carbon material and copper, which prevents separation of anode particles and ensures retention of the anode's mechanical and electrical integrity upon cycling. The swelling behavior of the poly(ionic liquid) binder in contact with 1&nbsp;M LiPF<sub>6</sub> EC:DEC/1&nbsp;M NaClO<sub>4</sub> EC:PC electrolyte was examined using two methods. First, the binder was added to the electrolyte and its solubility was observed after seven days. Second, a coated, calendared electrode containing the PMAI binder was immersed in the electrolyte for seven days and shaken. Images before and after seven days for both experiments are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information). It was observed that the binder did not dissolve in the electrolyte, and neither the active material nor the conductive carbon detached from the electrode surface. This indicates that the binder does not swell in the electrolyte medium.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403071-sec-0040-title">2.2 PMAI as Graphite Anode Binder: Electrochemical Performance in LIBs</h3>
            
            <p>In order to investigate the impact of binder's interactions with the active components and electrolytes on the electrochemical performances, CV measurements were performed for PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr. During the first cathodic sweep, the PMAI/Gr (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0003">3a</a>) and PVDF/Gr (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0003">3b</a>) displayed electrolyte reduction peaks around 0.6&nbsp;V and a distinctive lithiation peak at a low potential of ≈0.01&nbsp;V. The electrolyte decomposition on the graphite surface led to the formation of the SEI which facilitates Li<sup>+</sup> transport and prevents further electrolyte decomposition. In the consecutive scans, the electrolyte decomposition peaks do not exist indicating the formation of a stable SEI film. In the case of PMAI/Gr, the first cycle cathodic curve between 1.7&nbsp;V and 0.8&nbsp;V shows a reduction peak, while in PVDF/Gr, the first cycle curve overlaps with the subsequent cycles in the same range. This indicates that the PIL binder gets reduced before the electrolyte decomposition. The reduction corresponds to the vinyl group and the α-hydrogen between the nitrogen atoms of the imidazolium ring, leading to the formation of organic product imidazol-2-ylidene carbene as reported by Zamory et&nbsp;al. which serves as ion-hoping site.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0053_R_d164363756e762" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">53</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e762" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This helps in the formation of functionalized SEI which enhances the lithiation-delithiation process. On the other hand, the anodic peak located at 0.2&nbsp;V results from the delithiation process of graphite. The cathodic and anodic potential peak differences are similar for PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr which is 0.011/0.30. While the overpotential, calculated as the difference in the anodic peaks between 0.1&nbsp;mV sec<sup>−1</sup> and 1&nbsp;mV sec<sup>−1</sup> of CV for PMAI/Gr, was found to be lower (0.150&nbsp;V) than PVDF/Gr (0.196&nbsp;V) as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information). This indicates that the PIL binders facilitate faster Li<sup>+</sup> transport and lowers internal impedance.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ba28dd9d-e881-4808-a90c-008030bccfb6/aenm202403071-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/ba28dd9d-e881-4808-a90c-008030bccfb6/aenm202403071-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b94b5b40-ba0d-4abd-87ba-629d9fd373e3/aenm202403071-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ba28dd9d-e881-4808-a90c-008030bccfb6/aenm202403071-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">CV curves of a) PMAI/Gr and b) PVDF/Gr at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. c) Impedance curves of cycled PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr. Inset: Equivalent circuit for EIS fitting. d) Arrhenius plots of R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> at varied temperatures.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>To further study interphase impedance and Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient in graphite anode, EIS was carried out on cycled electrodes. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0003">3c</a> shows the Nyquist plots of the graphite-based anodic half-cells before and after CV studies, exhibiting a semicircle in the high to medium-frequency region and a linear line in the low-frequency range. The semicircle corresponds to charge transfer resistance across electrolyte/electrode interface (R<sub>CT</sub>) and SEI resistance (R<sub>SEI</sub>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0081" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0081_R_d164363756e815" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 81 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">81</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0082" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0082_R_d164363756e815" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 82 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">82</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The resistance values are listed in Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> according to equivalent circuit fitting of the curves using R<sub>s</sub>(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(CR<sub>CT</sub>)W, where R<sub>s</sub> stands for ohmic resistance, Q is the constant phase element, C is capacitance and W represents Warburg resistance. The lower R<sub>CT</sub> (21.9 Ω) observed in PMAI/Gr compared to PVDF/Gr (125.9 Ω) suggests that the dense polar functional group within the PIL binder could enhance the Li<sup>+</sup> conduction into the electrode domain. This improvement is attributed to the inherent ionic conductivity of the PIL binder, distinguishing it from PVDF. Furthermore, the PMAI/Gr showed a lower R<sub>SEI</sub> of 11.08 Ω than PVDF/Gr with 29.97 Ω, owing to PIL's influence in forming thin and stable SEI compared to PVDF. Thus, PMAI binder could ease graphite's expansion stress and accelerate the formation of stable SEI film.</p>
            
            <p>The ion diffusion coefficient and activation energy were measured to investigate the Li<sup>+</sup> kinetics at the SEI and electrode. A theoretical study in 1993 was carried out to minimize the internal resistance, revealing that Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion was constrained by the ability of ions to move in and out of active material.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0083" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0083_R_d164363756e846" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 83">83</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, the Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Li+</sub>) can be influenced by binder, which can affect the high power output. As mentioned in the experimental section, D<sub>Li+</sub> was analyzed from the low frequency region of the EIS curve after CV cycles. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information) shows the correlation between Z<sub>real</sub> (Z`) and ω<sup>−1/2</sup> of PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr in the low-frequency region. The D<sub>Li+</sub> is inversely proportional to the Warburg factor (σ<sup>2</sup>), obtained from the curve's slope shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information). The PMAI/Gr presents higher D<sub>Li+</sub> values of 1.03E-10 cm<sup>2</sup> sec<sup>−1</sup> which is two orders of magnitude larger than PVDF/Gr with 3.08E-12 cm<sup>2</sup> sec<sup>−1</sup>, boosting Li<sup>+</sup> mobility and better electrochemical performance. Further activation energies (E<sub>a</sub>)&nbsp;of PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr were calculated from EIS at different temperatures. The activation energy of charge transfer process signifies the energy barrier Li<sup>+</sup> must overcome when transitioning between electrolyte's solvation sphere and electrode interface. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information) shows the temperature-dependent Nyquist plots at lithiation state (≈0.1&nbsp;V) measured after CV. Equivalent circuit fitting of the impedance spectra was carried out using R<sub>s</sub>(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(QR<sub>CT</sub>)W to determine the R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> (Tables&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Xu et&nbsp;al. reported that the activation energy values change with the electrolyte compositions,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0084" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0084_R_d164363756e911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 84 - J. Mater. Res.">84</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0085" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0085_R_d164363756e911" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 85 - Electrochim. Acta">85</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> suggesting that E<sub>a</sub> at graphite depends on either Li<sup>+</sup> desolvation or the SEI nature or both. The activation energies for PMAI/Gr are calculated to be 42.0&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> and 36.2&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> for R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub>, respectively. These values are lower than those for PVDF/Gr with 62.7&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> and 62.1&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> for R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> respectively, as calculated from the Arrhenius plots shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0003">3d</a>. The Li<sup>+</sup> kinetic studies indicate that the interfaces formed in the PMAI/Gr facilitate diffusion through the electrode system, owing to PIL's dense polar groups, ionic conductivity and electrolyte adsorption, which enhances ion mobility during charge-discharge.</p>
            
            <p>The galvanostatic charge-discharge performance was investigated to analyze the binder's ability to perform long cycle life. The formation of the SEI during the initial lithiation process is attributed to an irreversible reduction reaction involving ethylene carbonate, occurring at around 0.6&nbsp;V. This phenomenon is clearly evident in the specific capacity versus voltage profile and the dQ/dV plot for both PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr, as illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0004">4</a>. Furthermore, a distinct PMAI reduction peak was observed in the 1.8-0.8&nbsp;V voltage range. The peak precedes the reduction of the electrolyte in both the charge-discharge curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0004">4a,b</a>) and the dQ/dV plot (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0004">4c,d</a>) of PMAI/Gr, which aligns with earlier observations recorded in CV curves. The peak is absent in the subsequent cycle due to the formation of a stable film on the surface of the electrode. Such binder reduction peaks are also not observed in most commercial binders such as CMC, PAA and SBR-containing electrodes as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information). Reduction of the insoluble PMAI binder at the interface can improve binder's adherence to graphite by forming chemical bonds upon reduction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0086" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0086_R_d164363756e961" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 86 - Inorg. Chem.">86</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5887459e-7234-4e6b-8a32-cc4edd488b77/aenm202403071-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/5887459e-7234-4e6b-8a32-cc4edd488b77/aenm202403071-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/45072527-7e3d-4f8c-be9c-0b0f7aed7249/aenm202403071-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5887459e-7234-4e6b-8a32-cc4edd488b77/aenm202403071-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Lithiation-delithiation voltage profiles at 0.1C rate of a) PMAI/Gr and b) PVDF/Gr. dQ/dV plots for first and second lithiation cycle at 0.1C rate of c) PMAI/Gr and d) PVDF/Gr.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The rate capability of the anodic half cells was measured by galvanostatic charge–discharge at increasing current densities. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information) summarizes the specific capacity of PMAI and PVDF binders from 0.1C to 2C. The specific capacity of PMAI/Gr are 344, 207, 112, 99, 96 and 71 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>at 0.1C, 0.2C, 0.5C, 0.75C, 1C and 2C respectively. While PVDF/Gr showed 281, 156, 95, 72, 66 and 44 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1C, 0.2C, 0.5C, 0.75C, 1C and 2C respectively. It can be studied that the water-processed PMAI binder delivers higher specific capacity values at all applied current densities than PVDF binder cells by boosting Li<sup>+</sup> transport in the electrode domain. Further investigation on long cycling capability was executed at 1C and 5C. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0005">5a</a> shows PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr cycling performances up to 800 cycles at 1C. PMAI/Gr achieved a maximum specific capacity of 297 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> with approximately 80% capacity retention of the maximum specific capacity after 750 cycles, while PVDF/Gr demonstrated a specific capacity of 228 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> with 72% capacity retention. Fast charging capability of the electrode materials was assessed at a high current density of 5C, which provides a harsh environment and accelerates the aging of the electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0005">5b</a>). PMAI/Gr exhibited a high specific capacity of 85 mAhg<sup>−1</sup>, while PVDF presents a low specific capacity 47 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> for 1000 cycles. The PMAI binder showed remarkable specific capacity at 5 C-rate due to the formation of nano heterojunction between PIL/electrolyte of the electrode surface, which enhances charge carrier mobility. The observed initial drop in specific capacity followed by its recovery is attributed to the activation process of active sites in graphite, a behavior consistent with earlier reported studies on graphite<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0002_R_d164363756e1016" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>. The drop in the capacity observed depends on the rate at which electrode decomposition, graphite exfoliation and electrode degradation take place. Wherein PMAI/Gr showed slower drop in specific capacity compared to PVDF/Gr. The increase of reduction species formed at the graphite electrode caused a decline in long-cycling performance in PVDF/Gr due to growth in SEI. In contrast, the high-capacity retention of PMAI/Gr at a high charging rate is linked to decreased reduction products formed between the electrode/electrolyte interface. It is evident that PMAI binder has influenced electrolyte reduction in cells and demonstrated better performance when compared to conventional PVDF binder.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/431e650d-7842-4a1c-b0a3-c099d7a3bf20/aenm202403071-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/431e650d-7842-4a1c-b0a3-c099d7a3bf20/aenm202403071-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cc422dcf-1c58-4295-88bc-7f12093d876b/aenm202403071-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/431e650d-7842-4a1c-b0a3-c099d7a3bf20/aenm202403071-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Galvanostatic cycling of PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr at a) 1C and b) 5C for 800 and 1000 cycles. R<sub>SEI</sub> versus voltage plots during c) lithiation and d) delithiation of cycled anodic half-cells.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Battery ageing was investigated using differential capacity analysis (DCA) to characterize the State of Health (SOH) through peak identification corresponding to phase transformations of active material. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information) shows the DCA curves of different cycles as dQ/dV versus V for PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr respectively during lithiation and delithiation. The main cause for fast capacity fading of PVDF/Gr was analyzed by dQ/dV curves. A shift in the peaks towards voltages and a decrease in the peak heights as the cycle number increases during both the lithiation and delithiation was observed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13c,d</a> (Supporting Information). This indicates that the PVDF/Gr undergoes conductivity loss due to loss of active material,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0087" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0087_R_d164363756e1052" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 87 - Electrochem. Solid-State Lett.">87</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> decomposition of electrolyte/SEI growth and lithium plating.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0088" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0088_R_d164363756e1057" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 88 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">88</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> No such difference in dQ/dV peak was observed during cycling of PMAI/Gr (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a,b</a>, Supporting Information), indicating no change in surface composition and loss of electronic pathway.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0089" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0089_R_d164363756e1066" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 89 - J. Power Sources">89</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The analysis showed the increased cell polarization resistance observed in PVDF/Gr cell upon cycling leading to capacity fade and degradation. Hence DCA analysis confirms that the PMAI binder helps in maintaining the structural integrity of the electrode and prevents parasitic reaction on the surface of the electrode.</p>
            
            <p>To gain further insight into the kinetics of Li<sup>+</sup> during different state of charge, dynamic electrochemical impedance spectroscopy on the cycled electrodes was measured at varied voltages. The Nyquist plots for PMAI and PVDF during lithiation and delithiation are plotted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information). The experimental impedance data was fitted using an equivalent circuit R<sub>s</sub>L(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(QR<sub>CT</sub>)(XR<sub>diff</sub>)W and the kinetic parameter is tabulated in Tables&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4–S7</a> (Supporting Information). Where X═Q or C and R<sub>diff</sub> represents diffusion resistance. The R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> influence the electrochemical performances of a cell as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0005">5c and d</a>. The R<sub>SEI</sub> values in PMAI/Gr during lithiation and delitiation are lower than PVDF/Gr indicating the formation of thin and stable SEI on the surface of PMAI/Gr electrode which protects and accommodates the volume change during cycling. In contrast, high R<sub>SEI</sub> values of PVDF/Gr are ascribed to poor influence of PVDF binder on SEI formation and structural integrity of electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0090" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0090_R_d164363756e1105" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 90 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">90</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0091" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0091_R_d164363756e1105" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 91 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">91</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The higher R<sub>SEI</sub> values in the lithiation voltage region than the rest of the voltage region of PMAI/Gr due to the Li concentration gradient within the electrode is more pronounced thereby hindering the lithiation process at the SEI and the electrode. The abrupt increase in R<sub>SEI</sub> values at ≈1&nbsp;V for both PMAI/Gr and PVDF/Gr electrodes may be attributed to the initiation of lithiation and the termination of delithiation processes. These events can result in changes in the concentration gradient on either side of the SEI and alterations in ionic mobility within the SEI, subsequently influencing the overall resistance of the cell.</p>
            
            <p>To investigate the surface chemistry of the cycled cells and understand the composition of the SEI, XPS analyses were performed on electrodes with different binders, including PMAI, PVDF, CMC, PAA, and SBR. The XPS signals for C 1s (≈284&nbsp;eV), O 1s (≈535&nbsp;eV), and F 1s (≈686&nbsp;eV) were recorded and are presented in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0006">6a, b</a>, and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information). The spectra for electrodes with CMC, PAA, and SBR binders are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a> (Supporting Information). Species concentrations calculated from the XPS data are summarized in Tables&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8–S10</a> (Supporting Information). For the PMAI/Gr, PVDF/Gr, CMC/Gr, PAA/Gr, and SBR/Gr electrodes, the C 1s spectra showed significant contributions from sp3 carbon at 284.6&nbsp;eV.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0092" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0092_R_d164363756e1133" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 92 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">92</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0093" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0093_R_d164363756e1133" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 93 - J. Phys. Chem. B">93</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> All electrodes exhibited SEI species resulting from electrolyte decomposition, including C<span class="icomoon"></span>O, C═O, and Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, with similar Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> concentrations for all the electrodes, except for SBR/Gr. However, PMAI/Gr displayed a higher concentration of C<span class="icomoon"></span>O species due to the overlap of C-N and C<span class="icomoon"></span>O peaks, as also observed in the N 1s spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0094" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0094_R_d164363756e1150" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 94 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">94</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This suggests that the reduction of the binder prior to electrolyte decomposition leads to the formation of an SEI containing nitrogen species, which facilitates Li<sup>+</sup> transport through the SEI while limiting Li<sup>+</sup> flux localization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0095" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0095_R_d164363756e1160" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 95 - Royal Soc. Chem.">95</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The C<span class="icomoon"></span>O and C═O peaks observed in the O 1s spectra confirm the presence of these species in the SEI, with PMAI/Gr, CMC/Gr, and PAA/Gr electrodes showing higher concentrations due to contributions from the binder. Notably, PMAI/Gr exhibited a higher concentration of Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> compared to other binders, likely due to the influence of its dense functional groups. In contrast, the non-functionalized SBR/Gr showed minimal influence on Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> formation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0096" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0096_R_d164363756e1174" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 96 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">96</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> F 1s spectra revealed the presence of Li<sub>x</sub>POF<sub>y</sub> and LiF in all electrodes except SBR/Gr, which only exhibited Li<sub>x</sub>POF<sub>y</sub>. The PMAI/Gr electrode, however, showed a high concentration of LiF. The absence of LiF species peak in SBR/Gr could be due to formation of thick organic layer. According to Zhang et&nbsp;al., inorganic species in the SEI, such as Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and LiF, provide mechanical and chemical protection while regulating Li<sup>+</sup> transport. Although Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and LiF have moderately low ionic conductivity, their interaction at interfaces can promote the accumulation of space charges, leading to a higher concentration of ionic carriers, enhanced Li<sup>+</sup> transport, and reduced electron leakage. Thus, the high concentration of LiF and Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> in PMAI/Gr contribute to improved current efficiency and long-term cycle stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0097" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0097_R_d164363756e1205" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 97 - Electrochem. Commun.">97</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In conclusion, the dense functional groups in the PMAI binder facilitate the formation of an SEI rich in inorganic species and nitrogen functionalities, enhancing electrochemical performance compared to commercial binders.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d1a34082-3a91-49a5-8079-b7ab47f80432/aenm202403071-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d1a34082-3a91-49a5-8079-b7ab47f80432/aenm202403071-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/23e4dc41-f973-4efa-a40c-f0d122a418ae/aenm202403071-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d1a34082-3a91-49a5-8079-b7ab47f80432/aenm202403071-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">C 1s XPS spectra of cycled a) PMAI/Gr and b) PVDF/Gr electrodes. Cross-sectional SEM images of cycled c) PMAI/Gr and d) PVDF/Gr electrodes.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The surface morphology and microenvironment of the pristine and aged graphite electrodes were studied using SEM to further investigate the effect of binder on graphite electrode structure and electrochemical stability. The SEM images of the pristine electrode surface are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a1,b1</a> (Supporting Information). As noted, the graphite particles displayed uniform distribution throughout the surface and interior of electrodes. After long cycling, the aged electrodes' surface SEM images represented in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a2,a3</a> (Supporting Information) showed a shining surface with no cracks in the PMAI-based electrode, indicating that the stable electrode structure inhibits particle degradation and enhances lithium mobility during cycling. In the PVDF-based electrodes, cracks and voids are formed across the surface which may hinder the Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion and increase the electrolyte decomposition (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18b2,b3</a>, Supporting Information). This supports the higher R<sub>SEI</sub> observed after fitting impedance, impacting electrochemical performances and Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient. On the cross-sectional image of aged electrodes, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0006">6c</a>, the graphite particles are evenly distributed and compact with no contact gap between the current collector and the graphite particles of aged PMAI-based electrodes. In comparison, the cross-sectional image of the aged PVDF-based electrode shows cracks in the electrode depth and loss of contact between the current collector and graphite particles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0006">6d</a>). Hence, electrode structure degradation probably induced the capacity loss observed in PVDF/Gr. The presence of PMAI binder is not solely located on base plains, but also aggregates at the edges, effectively bridging various graphene layers, thereby contributing to the prevention of exfoliation of graphite by acting as nano-scale stitches.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e1255" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It can be concluded that incorporating PMAI binder with ionic conductive properties, will enhance the Li<sup>+</sup> transport along the electrode and increase the specific capacity, thereby aiding cell performance and preserving electrode's integrity throughout cycling.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403071-sec-0050-title">2.3 PMAI as Hard Carbon Anode Binder: Electrochemical Performance in SIBs</h3>
            
            <p>The remarkable performance of LIBs using PMAI binder has motivated us to evaluate PMAI as a binder for HC anode in SIBs. To compare the impact of binders (PMAI and PVDF) on the HC material's electrochemical properties, we examined the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/deintercalation processes within the voltage range of 0.01-2.5&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na. This investigation includes cyclic voltammetry (CV), impedance spectroscopy and galvanostatic charge–discharge. The CV profiles of both PMAI/HC (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0007">7a</a>) and PVDF/HC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0007">7b</a>) at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> exhibit SEI formation peak at ≈0.5&nbsp;V in the first reduction cycle before Na<sup>+</sup> reduction at ≈0.1&nbsp;V. The Na<sup>+</sup> anodic/cathodic peaks of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC exhibited at 0.01/0.14&nbsp;V and 0.01/0.17&nbsp;V, respectively, suggest that PMAI/HC has lower polarization and faster ion kinetics than PVDF/HC. The second and third CV curves almost overlap, suggesting the absence of continuous electrolyte reduction and a stable SEI layer formation during the first cycle in both PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC. Additionally, only in PMAI/HC a broad peak was observed at ≈0.7&nbsp;V, corresponding to reduction of the imidazolium group within the binder,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e1291" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which precedes reduction of EC in the electrolyte, leading to the formation of functionalized SEI which might facilitate ion diffusion and limit excess electrolyte reduction. Binders play a significant role in the shape of the CV curve, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0007">7a,b</a>. PMAI/HC exhibits narrow redox peaks, while PVDF/HC shows broader redox peaks, emphasizing the influence of the ion-conductive binder on the electrode's electrochemical properties. CV curves of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC at different scan rates are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e7276da6-5bc7-4487-9e79-9880de9a404f/aenm202403071-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/e7276da6-5bc7-4487-9e79-9880de9a404f/aenm202403071-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/71898658-108a-4f3e-b52f-0bea9be5afb6/aenm202403071-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e7276da6-5bc7-4487-9e79-9880de9a404f/aenm202403071-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">CV profiles of a) PMAI/HC and b) PVDF/HC at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, Inset: Zoom in view of CV. c) EIS spectra of anodic half-cells. d) Arrhenius plot of SEI resistance and charge transfer resistance.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Further analysis was conducted to elucidate Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics at the interphase and electrode bulk. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0007">7c</a> shows the HC-based anodic half-cell Nyquist plots before and after CV studies. The resistance values are determined by circuit fitting of EIS curves, and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information) shows the fitting result using the circuit R<sub>s</sub>(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(QR<sub>CT</sub>)(QW). Both PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC showed a decrease in the diameter of the semicircle after CV, indicating a decrease in resistance due to the formation of SEI at the surface of the HC electrode.
