The circuit fitting analysis of EIS data of PMAI/HC after CV reveals relatively smaller resistances for R<sub>CT</sub> at 31.38 Ω and R<sub>SEI</sub> at 1.66 Ω compared to PVDF/HC, where R<sub>CT</sub> is 83.09 Ω and R<sub>SEI</sub> is 1.42 Ω. This observation suggests that the PMAI binder contributes to forming a thinner SEI, promoting favorable ion transfer processes and resulting in lower polarization. The binder's influence on the ion conductivity across the electrode domain was analyzed from the EIS data after CV, and the sodium diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na+</sub>) was calculated as already mentioned for LIB. The D<sub>Na+</sub> calculated value of PMAI/HC was 3.35E-13 cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, three times the value of PVDF/HC with 1.01E-13 cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> as calculated from the slope of Z` versus ω<sup>−1/2</sup> curves (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information). Here, the interfacial behavior influence the diffusion coefficient, attributed to the coupling of reduced charge transfer resistance, decrease in SEI layer resistance and ionic conductance promoted by PMAI in electrode domain. To investigate, the binder influence on SEI layer and interfacial kinetics, temperature-dependent EIS experiment was conducted to reveal ion diffusion kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0098" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0098_R_d164363756e1370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 98 - ACS Mater. Lett.">98</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0099" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0099_R_d164363756e1370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 99 - J. Power Sources">99</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The R<sub>CT</sub> and R<sub>SEI</sub> values are obtained by fitting the Nyquist curves (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information) using the circuit R<sub>s</sub>(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(QR<sub>CT</sub>)W. R<sub>CT</sub> values are usually larger than R<sub>SEI</sub>, and the resistance decreases as temperature increases (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12,S13</a>, Supporting Information). PMAI/HC showed lower R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> than PVDF/HC at different temperatures. The activation energy for Na<sup>+</sup> transport through SEI and electrolyte/electrode interface (charge transfer step) were calculated using the Arrhenius equation, illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0007">7d</a>. In PMAI/HC, E<sub>a</sub> due to SEI (E<sub>a</sub>,<sub>SEI</sub>) and charge transfer (E<sub>a</sub>,<sub>CT</sub>) are 47.43&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> and 50.21&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, which is lower than PVDF/HC with 52.70&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> and 56.61&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup> for E<sub>a</sub>,<sub>SEI</sub> and E<sub>a</sub>,<sub>CT</sub> respectively. The result indicated that Na<sup>+</sup> transport faces lower impedance at the interface of the PMAI containing electrode, which enhances faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion by better decoordination of solvent from Na-ion solvation complexes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0100" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0100_R_d164363756e1439" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 100 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">100</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0101" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0101_R_d164363756e1439" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 101 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">101</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Here, we propose that PMAI binder helps in the formation of a thin functional SEI, better ion conduction along edges of HC particles and facilitating desolvation of Na<sup>+</sup> at the interface by forming heterojunction between PIL and electrolyte.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0063_R_d164363756e1446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Macro Lett.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>In order to investigate the effect of binder on extended sodiation/desodiation of HC electrode, galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) was carried out. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0008">8a</a> shows long cycling charge/discharge specific capacities of the PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC at 60&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> after two cycles of precycling at 30&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>. The maximum specific capacity attended by PMAI/HC was 250 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 74%, which is higher than PVDF/HC with 178 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> and ICE of 47%. When precycling is performed at 30&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the number of cycles required to achieve a coulombic efficiency &gt;99% for PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC are the 6 and 9 cycles, respectively. The capacity retention with respect to initial specific capacity at 60&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> of PMAI/HC electrode after 200 cycles was calculated to be 96%, which is much higher than that of PVDF/HC at 88%. The rate capability of the anodic half cells containing different binders was tested at different current densities from 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> to 200&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0008">8b</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information). PMAI/HC shows better rate capability and delivers a specific capacity of 224 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> at 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> than PVDF/HC with 193 mAhg<sup>−1</sup>. In addition, PMAI/HC delivers a specific capacity of about 74 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> at 200&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>; the current density is 20 times higher than the initial current density and shows a higher capacity than PVDF/HC with 60 mAhg<sup>−1</sup>. GCD profiles of the first and second cycles of HC-based electrodes, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a> (Supporting Information), showed two clear regions of sodium storage processes and SEI formation in the first sodiation cycle. The two storage regions are sloping at high potential and plateau at low potential &lt;0.1&nbsp;V. Dahn et&nbsp;al. proposed an insertion-filling mechanism for sodium storage wherein the slope region from ≈1&nbsp;V to 0.1&nbsp;V is due to Na<sup>+</sup> insertion between parallel or nearly parallel layers, and the plateau corresponds to metal insertion into nanovoids.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0102" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0102_R_d164363756e1501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 102 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">102</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This was experimentally proved by Dhabi et&nbsp;al. using X-ray diffraction and pore size distribution.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0103" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0103_R_d164363756e1507" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 103 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">103</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The first sodiation curve does not overlap with the second sodiation, indicating electrolyte reduction reaction at the surface of HC electrode leading to formation of SEI during the first cycle. Further, dQ/dV plots at 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> were obtained to gain insight into the reduction, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0008">8c,d</a>. In the first sodiation process, PVDF/HC displays two apparent reduction peaks at 1.09&nbsp;V and 0.58&nbsp;V, which are ascribed to PC and EC decomposition, respectively and vanish in the following cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0104" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0104_R_d164363756e1517" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 104 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">104</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, PMAI/HC showed three peaks at 1.13&nbsp;V, 0.92&nbsp;V and 0.61&nbsp;V in the first sodiation cycle. Where 1.13&nbsp;V and 0.61&nbsp;V are solvent reduction peaks, while 0.92&nbsp;V corresponds to binder reduction as initially indicated by the CV studies. This binder reduction peak is absent in most commercial binders, such as those in CMC, PAA, and SBR-containing HC electrodes, as shown in dQ/dV plots Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> (Supporting Information). Zamory et&nbsp;al. mentioned that imidazolium-based IL undergoes reduction when combined with a low operating potential electrode, which can be taken advantage of when employing non-soluble PIL; the reduction reaction occurs between PIL binder and other components of electrode helping in binder adhesion to HC by chemical bonding.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0068_R_d164363756e1526" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - J. Power Sources">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hence, PMAI binder helps form functional SEI containing reduced binder product which facilitates Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/deintercalation and stability of the electrode during extended cycling. Differential capacity analysis was performed to investigate battery ageing and characterize the State of Health by peak change identification. The dQ/dV curves at different cycles of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information). The peak intensity steadily diminishes in PVDF/HC electrode, whereas the peak intensity remains relatively unchanged for PMAI/HC electrode. This indicates that PVDF binder-containing electrode undergoes loss of conductivity due to active material loss, which is consistent with cycling stability difference compared to the absence of such an observation with PMAI binder.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0087" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0087_R_d164363756e1537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 87 - Electrochem. Solid-State Lett.">87</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0089" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0089_R_d164363756e1537" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 89 - J. Power Sources">89</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d1b4ecf7-b8f9-4700-975c-4a3ad2faa89a/aenm202403071-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d1b4ecf7-b8f9-4700-975c-4a3ad2faa89a/aenm202403071-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ef573533-621f-449e-aa13-32aecc2c02f7/aenm202403071-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d1b4ecf7-b8f9-4700-975c-4a3ad2faa89a/aenm202403071-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Long cycling stability performance at 60&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC. b) Rate performance at varied current densities. dQ/dV plots obtained from galvanostatic profiles at 10&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> of c) PMAI/HC and d) PVDF/HC.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The impedance to Na<sup>+</sup> kinetics at different potentials in the 0.01&nbsp;V–2.5&nbsp;V range was determined using dynamic electrochemical impedance spectroscopy on cycled electrode. The PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC Nyquist plots during sodiation and desodiation are plotted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> (Supporting Information). An equivalent circuit R<sub>s</sub>L(QR<sub>SEI</sub>)(QR<sub>CT</sub>)(XR<sub>diff</sub>)W which fits with a high chi-square value, was used on impedance profile and the resistance value is tabulated in Tables&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15–S18</a> (Supporting Information). The PMAI/HC exhibits lower R<sub>CT</sub> (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0009">9a,c</a>) and R<sub>SEI</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0009">9b,d</a>) than PVDF/HC at corresponding sodiation and desodiation potential. Further confirming the formation of thin SEI by the influence and reduction of PMAI binder, and the presence of polar groups in PMAI facilitates Na<sup>+</sup> transport at the electrolyte/electrode interface. The stable R<sub>SEI</sub> values along the potential range indicate that PMAI/HC contains stable SEI at the HC electrode surface at different potentials and confirms better electrode electrochemical reversibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0052_R_d164363756e1604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">52</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0090" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0090_R_d164363756e1604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 90 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">90</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0091" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0091_R_d164363756e1604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 91 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">91</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, R<sub>CT</sub> values during sodiation are higher than desodiation in both PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC. This might be due to increased resistance of Na<sup>+</sup> during deeper penetration into electrode structure and the impact of Na<sup>+</sup> flux, whereas during desodiation, the structure becomes more relaxed, leading to lower R<sub>CT</sub>. In addition, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion during sodiation into the electrode might be a limiting factor, which is facile during desodiation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0041_R_d164363756e1620" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0053_R_d164363756e1620" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The unstable and higher R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>CT</sub> values of PVDF/HC might be due to continuous decomposition of electrolyte and also uneven SEI on electrode surface.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/a583f762-99d4-4ce3-95ec-0441bc69312a/aenm202403071-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/a583f762-99d4-4ce3-95ec-0441bc69312a/aenm202403071-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e611af47-9776-483a-ad23-a17f5c1ff603/aenm202403071-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/a583f762-99d4-4ce3-95ec-0441bc69312a/aenm202403071-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) R<sub>CT</sub> and b) R<sub>SEI</sub> values during sodiation of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC. (a) R<sub>CT</sub> and (b) R<sub>SEI</sub> values during desodiation of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC. C 1s XPS spectra of cycled electrodes containing e) PMAI and f) PVDF binders.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Chemical analysis of HC surface was examined using XPS to understand the SEI film's chemical structure after long cycling of electrodes. Cycled PMAI/HC, PVDF/HC, CMC/HC, PAA/HC and SBR/HC electrodes were analyzed to understand binders' influence on SEI composition. The concentration percentage of each species composition is tabulated in Tables&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information). The C 1s, O 1s and Cl 2p XPS results of cycle electrodes are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0009">9e, f</a>; Figures&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26, S27</a> (Supporting Information). All the anodic half cells contain sp3 C-C, C═O, C<span class="icomoon"></span>O and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> species at the SEI as seen in C 1s spectra.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0069_R_d164363756e1678" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Adv. Energy Mater.">69</a>-<a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0071_R_d164363756e1678" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However the PVDF/HC electrode showed a C-F peak, due to the binder containing C-F bond, whereas PMAI/HC electrode showed the presence of C═C and C-N peaks. The presence of a C═C peak originates from the binder reduction product containing imidazolium units at SEI, which helps in ionic conduction along SEI during high Na<sup>+</sup> flux at sodiation potential range. The overlap of C-N peak with C<span class="icomoon"></span>O peak was confirmed by the O 1s spectra concentration analysis and N 1s spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0094" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0094_R_d164363756e1689" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 94 - J. Mater. Chem. A Mater.">94</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0096" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0096_R_d164363756e1689" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 96 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">96</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The C-N/C<span class="icomoon"></span>O species is of higher concentration in C 1s spectra, while in O 1s spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26a</a>, Supporting Information), the C<span class="icomoon"></span>O and C═O species concentrations are the same, confirming the two peaks' overlap.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0069_R_d164363756e1697" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Adv. Energy Mater.">69</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0071_R_d164363756e1697" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This also confirmed the reduction of binder and presence of C-N species at the SEI, enhancing Na<sup>+</sup> transport along the SEI. The higher concentration of C<span class="icomoon"></span>O and C═O species from the O 1s spectra of PMAI/HC electrode might be from the contribution of the binder. The SEI of PVDF/HC, CMC/HC, PAA/HC, and SBR/HC electrodes is rich in inorganic species like Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>2</sub>O, primarily due to the dissolution of the organic layer, exposing the inner inorganic components.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0105" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0105_R_d164363756e1711" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 105 - ACS Energy Lett.">105</a>, <a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0106_R_d164363756e1711" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Nano Energy">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This phenomenon is more pronounced in SIBs, as sodium forms less stable organometallic compounds compared to lithium. Lithium's higher charge density makes it a more effective initiator of anionic polymerization, leading to a more cross-linked, stable, and less soluble SEI in LIBs. In contrast, in the case of SIB, SEI is less cross-linked and more prone to dissolution, leaving them vulnerable to further degradation. Functional binders like PMAI, CMC, and PAA show lower inorganic species content in the SEI compared to PVDF and SBR, indicating that the organic layer formed is more stable due to the influence of these functional binders. Increasing the density of functional groups and binder reduction on the electrode surface, as seen with the imidazolium group in PMAI, can lead to a more stable organic layer in the SEI of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0107_R_d164363756e1717" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>The morphology of HC electrodes with different binders after long cycling charge/discharge studies was investigated using SEM. Pristine electrodes containing different binders showed a uniform distribution of HC on the current collector, as shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0010">10a</a> and <a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0010">d</a>. A significant change in morphology was observed in PMAI/HC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0010">10b</a>) and PVDF/HC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0010">10e</a>) electrodes after cycling in terms of visible film formation. PVDF/HC showed cracks on the surface, facilitating thick SEI formation, and leading to continuous decomposition of electrolyte and sodium consumption. Moreover, the thick closed membranous film will significantly affect Na-ion migration along the SEI film, thus hindering cycling performance. The cracks on the surface also signify that the PVDF binder provides weak adhesion between HC particles, leading to poor capacity and stability of the electrode. Nevertheless, the PMAI/HC electrode maintains better structural integrity after cycling, confirming the effect of dense polar functional groups in facilitating adhesion with and between the particles. Besides, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0010">10c</a> and f present cross-section images of PMAI/HC and PVDF/HC electrodes. When PMAI serves as binder, no gap or cracks are observed within the electrode and between the electrode and current collector, as seen in PVDF/HC electrode. This gap eventually leads to ion and electron conductivity loss and will widen during extended cycling. Hence, the reduced PMAI binder improves adhesion with copper foil and electrode stability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/dca67af4-1681-4f0e-a189-f8f14f194fbb/aenm202403071-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/dca67af4-1681-4f0e-a189-f8f14f194fbb/aenm202403071-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1191308f-84e9-40a8-b51e-268fc03b7eb2/aenm202403071-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/dca67af4-1681-4f0e-a189-f8f14f194fbb/aenm202403071-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 10<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) and d) pristine electrode containing PMAI and PVDF binder respectively. Top view of cycled b) PMAI and e) PVDF binder containing electrodes. Cross-section view of cycled c) PMAI and f) PVDF binder-containing electrodes.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403071-sec-0060-title">2.4 PMAI's Practical Potential for High-Loading and Full-Cell Applications</h3>
            
            <p>To further explore PMAI as a binder for commercial application, high-loading anodic half cells and coin-type full cells were assembled and studied. A high active mass loading of 8.2&nbsp;mg cm⁻<sup>2</sup> and 7.8&nbsp;mg cm⁻<sup>2</sup> was utilized for LIB and SIB negative electrodes respectively in anodic half-cells. The long-term galvanostatic charge-discharge performance of PMAI/Gr and PMAI/HC electrodes is shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0011">11a,b</a>. These high-mass-loading electrodes demonstrated exceptional cycling stability, maintaining a capacity of 1.10 mAh at 0.2C after 100 cycles for PMAI/Gr and 1.23 mAh at 60&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> after 50 cycles for PMAI/HC. Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a> (Supporting Information) illustrates the selected voltage profiles from the cyclic study for both LIB and SIB. Typically, active materials suffer from poor mechanical stability due to expansion and contraction during cycling, along with the binder's inability to hold the active material together, which negatively impacts battery performance as mass loading increases. However, PMAI-containing electrodes exhibited remarkable stability, avoiding electrode breakage even at high mass loading. This underscores the superior adhesion properties of PMAI, effectively mitigating volume changes and ensuring consistent performance.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403071-fig-0011"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/249b3e75-4756-4d96-ab9f-a2bec08485af/aenm202403071-fig-0011-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/249b3e75-4756-4d96-ab9f-a2bec08485af/aenm202403071-fig-0011-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/69ce3c7d-a75d-4163-9e6f-6e613096ad56/aenm202403071-fig-0011-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/249b3e75-4756-4d96-ab9f-a2bec08485af/aenm202403071-fig-0011-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 11<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403071-fig-0011&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403071" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Charge-discharge study of high active mass loading anodic half-cells for a) PMAI/Gr and b) PMAI/HC. Cycling performance of c) NMC622 //PMAI-Gr-based full cell and d) NVP//PMAI-HC-based full cell.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Encouraged by the high-loading half-cell performance, we further explored the practical applicability by assembling full cells, pairing PMAI-containing anodes with LiNi<sub>6</sub>Mn<sub>2</sub>Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NMC622) for LIBs and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) for SIBs. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0011">11c,d</a> illustrate the discharge capacity variation over cycles for the NMC622//PMAI-Gr and NVP//PMAI-HC full cells respectively. NMC622//PMAI-Gr cell exhibited an initial discharge capacity of ≈1.0 mAh, retaining nearly 80% of this capacity after 100 cycles. Whereas NVP//PMAI-HC cell exhibited an initial discharge capacity of ≈1.1 mAh, retaining nearly 65% of this capacity after 50 cycles, showcasing PMAI's effectiveness as a binder in practical full-cell applications. Selected voltage profiles from the cyclic study of LIB and SIB are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a> (Supporting Information). Furthermore, these full cells successfully powered an LED setup, as depicted in the inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403071-fig-0011">11c,d</a>, reinforcing PMAI's potential as a binder for future applications in metal-ion secondary batteries.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403071-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, a novel water-soluble poly(oxycarbonylmethylene 1-allyl-3-methyimidazolium (PMAI), containing high-density imidazolium functional groups, was synthesized and characterized using NMR and FT-IR. PMAI was evaluated as a binder using an aqueous processing method for battery electrode fabrication of LIBs/SIBs, offering a more sustainable and cost-effective alternative to the conventional organic-processed PVDF. Dense polar imidazolium-based functional group enhances affinity with electrolyte solvent and increase the Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient along the electrode domain. The CV, charge–discharge profile, and dQ/dV analyses have consistently demonstrated that PMAI gets reduced before that of ethylene carbonate in PMAI based LIB/SIB. This unique behavior is crucial in forming a stable and thin SEI enriched with inorganic and C-N species. The resulting SEI layer fosters reduced SEI resistance and contributes to lower activation energy and decreased overpotential, collectively enhancing the electrochemical performance and efficiency compared to PVDF-based LIB/SIB. PMAI/Gr showed enhanced long cycling performances with higher capacity retention of 80% after 750 cycles at 1C with a maximum specific capacity of 297 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> than PVDF/Gr. In addition, PMAI/Gr demonstrated superior charge-discharge at a 5C fast charging rate with a maximum specific capacity of 85 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> for 100 cycles, whereas PMAI/HC demonstrates a high specific capacity of 250 mAhg<sup>−1</sup>, exhibiting capacity retention of 96.2% with respect to initial specific capacity at 60 mAg<sup>−1</sup> current density after 200 cycles. This can be elucidated by the greater ionic conductivity and enhanced electrolyte adsorption exhibited by PMAI-based anodic half-cells. These properties further increase lithium mobility within the electrodes. Postmortem analysis on the aged electrode reveals a crackless uniform surface on the PMAI/Gr and PMAI/HC electrode, in contrast to PVDF/Gr and PVDF/HC electrode. The difference can be attributed to the exceptional peel strength observed by the PMAI binder in the peel test. In addition, high loading of active material and full cells were fabricated using PMAI as binder for negative electrode in LIB and SIB to demonstrate the potential for practical applications. The results not only establish PMAI as a better binder for replacing PVDF in LIB/SIB but also act as a catalyst in exploring deeper into the mechanisms of densely functional group polymers that underlie the unique functionality of PIL binders in the enhanced electrochemical performance.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403071-sec-0080-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0090">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0100">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403071-sec-0110-title"> Poly(ionic liquid) Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>PMAI was synthesized from ion exchange with the polymer poly(hydroxycarbonylmethylene) (PHCM) which was derived from poly(ethoxycarbonylmethylene) (PECM). PECM was synthesized following this previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403071-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403071-bib-0076_R_d164363756e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> PHCM was synthesized by base hydrolysis of PECM by refluxing a solution containing EtOH:H<sub>2</sub>O (2:1) and excess of KOH (Wako) for 24 hr. After the completion of the reaction, the reaction mixture was acidified upon adding 1N HCl (Sigma-Aldrich, 12N) and dialyzed using Fisherbrand regenerated cellulose dialysis tubing. Following water from the resulting solution was vacuum evaporated to yield PHCM. 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium hydroxide was synthesized via anion exchange of 2 gm of 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium chloride (AmImCl) dissolved in 100&nbsp;ml water using amberlite IRN78 OH hydroxide form (Supelco) column. Water was evaporated from the aqueous 1-allyl-3-methylimidazolium hydroxide (AmImOH) and dried overnight under a vacuum at 60&nbsp;°C. PHCM (200&nbsp;mg) and AmImOH (482&nbsp;mg) were dissolved in water and stirred overnight at room temperature. Finally, the product was vacum dried after evaporating water from the aqueous PMAI and washing with acetone. The yield of PMAI polymer was 78%. <sup>1</sup>H NMR (δ, ppm; D<sub>2</sub>O): 2.98 (C<b>H</b>COO-, 1H), 8.29 (1H, NC<b>H</b>N), 7.27 (2H, NC<b>H</b>C<b>H</b>N), 5.05 (2H, CH<sub>2</sub> = CHC<b>H</b><sub>2</sub>), 5.88 (1H, CH<sub>2</sub> = C<b>H</b>CH<sub>2</sub>), 5.25 (2H, C<b>H</b><sub>2</sub> = CHCH<sub>2</sub>), 3.77(3H, NC<b>H</b><sub>3</sub>). <sup>13</sup>C NMR (δ, ppm; D<sub>2</sub>O): 35.6, 51.0, 61.8, 119.4, 120.8, 122.3, 123.5, 130.7, 172.1.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403071-sec-0120-title"> Electrode Preparation and Cell Assembling</h4>
                  
                  <p>80 wt% battery grade graphite (Sigma-Aldrich) for LIB or HC (Kuranode Type 2 (5&nbsp;µm)) for SIB, 10 wt% super p conductive carbon (Alfa Aesar) and 10 wt% binders (PMAI or PVDF) were mixed using a solvent (water for PMAI and NMP for PVDF) to form a homogenous slurry, which was coated on copper foil using doctor blade (100&nbsp;µm) and dried under vacuum at 80&nbsp;°C for 24 hr. respectively. Subsequently, the dried coated electrodes were cut into 15&nbsp;mm discs. For SIB, CR2025 coin cells were fabricated using 1&nbsp;M NaClO<sub>4</sub> in ethylene carbonate (EC)/propylene carbonate (PC) electrolyte, glass fiber (Whatman) as separator and sodium disc as a counter electrode. Whereas for LIB, coin cells of CR2025 were assembled with polypropylene as separator wetted with 70 µl of 1&nbsp;M LiPF<sub>6</sub> in EC/DEC (1:1 v/v) (Sigma-Aldrich) electrolyte and lithium disc as counter electrodes. The cells were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox with 0.5 ppm &lt; H<sub>2</sub>O and 0.5 ppm &lt; O<sub>2</sub> atmosphere content. The PMAI binder-based anodic half cells were named PMAI/Gr for LIB and PMAI/HC for SIB, while PVDF binder-based anodic half cells were named PVDF/Gr for LIB and PVDF/HC for SIB.</p>
                  
                  <p>In the full-cell configuration for LIBs, graphite electrodes containing PMAI were used as the negative electrode, while commercial LiNi<sub>6</sub>Mn<sub>2</sub>Co<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NMC622, 1.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, PT-EdC62M15m-20P05-1, Piotrek) served as the positive electrode. For SIBs, the PMAI-containing hard carbon electrode was employed as the negative electrode, paired with a sodium vanadium phosphate (NVP, Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, NVP-20um, MTI) as positive electrode. The NVP electrode was composed of 80% NVP, 10% Super P conductive carbon, and 10% PVDF, and was coated on carbon-coated aluminum foil using NMP as the solvent. Prior to full-cell assembly, the negative electrodes underwent precycling in anodic half-cells with Li/Na foil as both the counter and reference electrode. This precycling step was beneficial for activating the electrodes and reducing the initial irreversible loss of Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup>-ions in the full-cell configuration. Following this activation, the precycled electrodes were used to assemble NMC622//PMAI-Gr and NVP//PMAI-HC full-cells. These full cells were cycled within a potential range of 2.8–4.2&nbsp;V for LIBs and 2.5–4.0&nbsp;V for SIBs. To prevent lithium or sodium metal plating on the negative electrode, the N/P ratio was maintained &gt; 1.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403071-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403071-sec-0130-title"> Synthetic and Electrochemical Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>PMAI chemical structure was analyzed using <sup>1</sup>H NMR and <sup>13</sup>C NMR (Bruker Advance II-400&nbsp;MHz spectrometer). Further FT-IR spectroscopy (PerkinElmer 100 FTIR spectrometer) was used to evaluate functional groups of the polymer. The thermal stability of the binder was determined using thermogravimetric analysis (TGA, Hitachi STA7200 thermal analysis system) under N<sub>2</sub> flow at a 10&nbsp;°C min<sup>−1</sup> heating rate. Binder adhesion strength was tested by peel test using Instron 3342 apparatus. A 40&nbsp;mm length coated electrode was affixed with adhesive tape on the coated side and peeled at a displacement rate of 2&nbsp;mm min<sup>−1</sup> at 180°. Moreover, Biologic Science Instruments measured cyclic voltammetry (CV) at different rates from 0.1 to 1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> between 0.01 and 2.1&nbsp;V versus Li<sup>+</sup>/Li for LIB and 0.01 and 2.5&nbsp;V versus Na<sup>+</sup>/Na for SIB. The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was performed at frequencies ranging from 1mHz to 1&nbsp;MHz using Biologic Science Instruments at a voltage amplitude of 10&nbsp;mV. The galvanostatic charge-discharge curves were obtained from Electrofield ABE1024 at different current densities. Microstructure morphology was observed by SEM (using Hitachi S-4500) at an accelerating voltage of 1.0&nbsp;kV. The elemental analysis and chemical bonding formation were analyzed using X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (Fisons instruments S-probe TM 2803).</p>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">From the EIS data at low-frequency domain, the Warburg factor (σ) was obtained from the Randles equation by plotting the real impedance versus square root of angular frequency (ω<sup>−1/2</sup>)

                     <div class="inline-equation" id="aenm202403071-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
